## Chapter: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study



### Introduction



In today's world, military intervention by great powers has become a common occurrence. Whether it is in the form of peacekeeping missions, humanitarian aid, or full-scale military operations, the media plays a crucial role in shaping public perception and understanding of these interventions. In this chapter, we will delve into the complex relationship between the media and great power military intervention. We will explore how the media influences public opinion, how it can be used as a tool by governments to justify intervention, and the impact of media coverage on the success or failure of interventions. Through a comprehensive study, we will gain a deeper understanding of the role of the media in shaping our understanding of great power military intervention. 





### Section: 11.1 Media as a Tool of Intervention:



The media plays a crucial role in shaping public opinion and understanding of great power military intervention. In this section, we will explore how the media can be used as a tool by governments to justify intervention and how it influences public perception of these interventions.



#### 11.1a Media and Public Opinion



The media has the power to shape public opinion through its coverage of great power military intervention. By selectively reporting on certain aspects of an intervention, the media can influence how the public perceives the intervention and its goals. This is especially true in the case of humanitarian interventions, where the media often focuses on the suffering of civilians and the need for intervention, rather than the political motivations behind the intervention.



One way in which the media can be used as a tool of intervention is through the dissemination of propaganda. Governments may use the media to spread biased or false information in order to gain public support for an intervention. This was seen in the lead up to the Iraq War in 2003, where the US government used the media to justify their invasion by spreading false information about weapons of mass destruction.



In addition to propaganda, the media can also influence public opinion through its framing of an intervention. Framing refers to the way in which the media presents information and shapes the narrative surrounding an event. By framing an intervention as a necessary and justifiable action, the media can sway public opinion in favor of the intervention. On the other hand, framing an intervention as an unjustified and aggressive act can turn public opinion against it.



The media also has the power to influence public opinion through its coverage of casualties and human suffering. By highlighting the suffering of civilians and soldiers, the media can create a sense of urgency and moral obligation for intervention. This was seen in the case of the Syrian Civil War, where the media's coverage of the humanitarian crisis led to increased pressure for intervention from the international community.



However, the media's influence on public opinion is not always straightforward. In some cases, the media's coverage of an intervention may have unintended consequences. For example, the media's focus on casualties and human suffering may lead to public backlash and opposition to an intervention. This was seen in the case of the Vietnam War, where the media's coverage of the war's brutality and high casualty rates turned public opinion against the intervention.



In conclusion, the media plays a significant role in shaping public opinion and understanding of great power military intervention. Governments can use the media as a tool to justify intervention and influence public perception, but the media's influence is not always predictable. As such, it is important to critically analyze media coverage of interventions and consider the potential biases and agendas at play. 





### Section: 11.1 Media as a Tool of Intervention:



The media plays a crucial role in shaping public opinion and understanding of great power military intervention. In this section, we will explore how the media can be used as a tool by governments to justify intervention and how it influences public perception of these interventions.



#### 11.1a Media and Public Opinion



The media has the power to shape public opinion through its coverage of great power military intervention. By selectively reporting on certain aspects of an intervention, the media can influence how the public perceives the intervention and its goals. This is especially true in the case of humanitarian interventions, where the media often focuses on the suffering of civilians and the need for intervention, rather than the political motivations behind the intervention.



One way in which the media can be used as a tool of intervention is through the dissemination of propaganda. Governments may use the media to spread biased or false information in order to gain public support for an intervention. This was seen in the lead up to the Iraq War in 2003, where the US government used the media to justify their invasion by spreading false information about weapons of mass destruction.



In addition to propaganda, the media can also influence public opinion through its framing of an intervention. Framing refers to the way in which the media presents information and shapes the narrative surrounding an event. By framing an intervention as a necessary and justifiable action, the media can sway public opinion in favor of the intervention. On the other hand, framing an intervention as an unjustified and aggressive act can turn public opinion against it.



The media also has the power to influence public opinion through its coverage of casualties and human suffering. By highlighting the suffering of civilians and soldiers, the media can create a sense of urgency and moral obligation for intervention. This was seen in the coverage of the Syrian Civil War, where images of children suffering from chemical attacks sparked international outrage and calls for intervention.



### Subsection: 11.1b Media and Policy Making



In addition to shaping public opinion, the media also plays a role in the policy making process. Policymakers often use the media to build support for their agendas and to shape public perception of their actions.



One way in which policymakers use the media is through the negotiation of newsworthiness. This refers to the interaction between journalists and sources to determine what is covered in the press and how it is presented. Policymakers hold a structural advantage in this process, as they are reliable sources of news and can use their influence to promote their own agendas.



Furthermore, policymakers may also use the media to disseminate their own propaganda and shape the narrative surrounding an intervention. By controlling the information that is presented to the public, policymakers can influence public opinion and build support for their actions.



The media also plays a role in agenda building for policymakers. Agenda building, a concept related to agenda setting, refers to the process of shaping the perceptions of policymakers and how they form their agendas. The media can influence this process by highlighting certain issues and framing them in a way that aligns with the policymakers' goals.



In conclusion, the media is a powerful tool in the process of great power military intervention. It can shape public opinion, influence policy making, and play a role in agenda building for policymakers. As such, it is important to critically analyze media coverage of interventions and consider the potential biases and agendas at play.





### Section: 11.1 Media as a Tool of Intervention:



The media plays a crucial role in shaping public opinion and understanding of great power military intervention. In this section, we will explore how the media can be used as a tool by governments to justify intervention and how it influences public perception of these interventions.



#### 11.1a Media and Public Opinion



The media has the power to shape public opinion through its coverage of great power military intervention. By selectively reporting on certain aspects of an intervention, the media can influence how the public perceives the intervention and its goals. This is especially true in the case of humanitarian interventions, where the media often focuses on the suffering of civilians and the need for intervention, rather than the political motivations behind the intervention.



One way in which the media can be used as a tool of intervention is through the dissemination of propaganda. Governments may use the media to spread biased or false information in order to gain public support for an intervention. This was seen in the lead up to the Iraq War in 2003, where the US government used the media to justify their invasion by spreading false information about weapons of mass destruction.



In addition to propaganda, the media can also influence public opinion through its framing of an intervention. Framing refers to the way in which the media presents information and shapes the narrative surrounding an event. By framing an intervention as a necessary and justifiable action, the media can sway public opinion in favor of the intervention. On the other hand, framing an intervention as an unjustified and aggressive act can turn public opinion against it.



The media also has the power to influence public opinion through its coverage of casualties and human suffering. By highlighting the suffering of civilians and soldiers, the media can create a sense of urgency and moral obligation for intervention. This was seen in the coverage of the Syrian Civil War, where images and videos of the suffering of civilians, particularly children, sparked international outrage and calls for intervention.



#### 11.1b Media and Government Control



In addition to shaping public opinion, the media can also be controlled by governments to further their own agendas. In some cases, governments may censor or restrict media coverage of an intervention in order to control the narrative and prevent negative perceptions. This was seen in the Chinese government's control of media coverage during the Tiananmen Square protests in 1989.



Furthermore, governments may also use the media to distract from domestic issues or to rally support for an intervention. This was seen in the US government's use of media coverage of the Gulf War in 1991 to distract from domestic economic issues and to boost national pride and support for the intervention.



#### 11.1c Case Studies



To further understand the role of media in great power military intervention, let us examine two case studies: the 1999 NATO intervention in Kosovo and the 2011 NATO intervention in Libya.



In the case of Kosovo, the media played a crucial role in shaping public opinion and justifying the intervention. The media coverage focused on the suffering of civilians and the need for intervention to stop ethnic cleansing by Serbian forces. This framing of the intervention as a humanitarian mission garnered widespread public support and helped to justify NATO's actions.



On the other hand, the media coverage of the intervention in Libya was more complex. While initial coverage focused on the need for intervention to protect civilians from the oppressive regime of Muammar Gaddafi, as the conflict continued, the media also highlighted the civilian casualties and destruction caused by NATO airstrikes. This led to a shift in public opinion and criticism of the intervention, with some arguing that it had gone beyond its initial humanitarian goals.



These case studies demonstrate the power of media in shaping public perception and support for great power military intervention. It also highlights the importance of critically analyzing media coverage and understanding the potential biases and agendas behind it.





### Section: 11.2 Media Critiques and Challenges:



The media plays a crucial role in shaping public opinion and understanding of great power military intervention. However, it is not without its flaws and criticisms. In this section, we will explore some of the critiques and challenges faced by the media in its coverage of intervention.



#### 11.2a Media Bias



One of the most prominent critiques of the media is its perceived bias. Bias refers to the tendency of the media to favor one side or perspective over another. In the United States, there have been numerous claims of a liberal bias in the media, particularly in politics. This bias is often attributed to the personal beliefs and political leanings of journalists and media outlets.



The issue of media bias is not a new one. In fact, it has been a topic of discussion since the 1960s when Senator Barry Goldwater, a conservative, alleged liberal bias during his presidential campaign. Since then, conservative media critics have continued to claim that the US media skews towards the political left.



However, it is important to note that bias is not limited to one side of the political spectrum. Studies have shown that both liberal and conservative biases exist in the media, and that commentary and opinion pieces are often more biased than factual news reporting. This blurring of lines between commentary and journalism has raised concerns about the objectivity and credibility of the media.



To address these concerns, there has been a growth of independent fact-checking and algorithms to assess bias. These efforts aim to hold the media accountable and provide a more balanced and accurate portrayal of events.



#### 11.2b Challenges of Objectivity



Another challenge faced by the media is the issue of objectivity. Objectivity refers to the ability of the media to present information without bias or personal opinion. However, in reality, achieving complete objectivity is nearly impossible. Journalists are human and are influenced by their own beliefs and experiences, which can unintentionally affect their reporting.



Furthermore, the media is often under pressure to produce stories quickly and attract viewers or readers. This can lead to sensationalism and the prioritization of certain stories over others. In the context of intervention, this can result in biased or incomplete coverage of events.



#### 11.2c The Role of Social Media



In recent years, the rise of social media has also posed challenges for the media. With the ability for anyone to share information and opinions online, it has become increasingly difficult to distinguish between fact and fiction. This has led to the spread of misinformation and the rise of "fake news."



In the context of intervention, social media can also be used as a tool for propaganda and manipulation. Governments and other actors can use social media to spread biased or false information to sway public opinion in favor of or against an intervention.



#### 11.2d The Need for Critical Analysis



Given these challenges, it is important for individuals to critically analyze the information presented by the media. This involves fact-checking, seeking out multiple sources, and being aware of potential biases. It is also important for the media to be transparent about their sources and methods of reporting.



In conclusion, while the media plays a crucial role in shaping public opinion and understanding of intervention, it is not without its flaws and challenges. It is important for both the media and individuals to be aware of these challenges and strive for accurate and objective reporting.





### Section: 11.2 Media Critiques and Challenges:



The media plays a crucial role in shaping public opinion and understanding of great power military intervention. However, it is not without its flaws and criticisms. In this section, we will explore some of the critiques and challenges faced by the media in its coverage of intervention.



#### 11.2a Media Bias



One of the most prominent critiques of the media is its perceived bias. Bias refers to the tendency of the media to favor one side or perspective over another. In the United States, there have been numerous claims of a liberal bias in the media, particularly in politics. This bias is often attributed to the personal beliefs and political leanings of journalists and media outlets.



The issue of media bias is not a new one. In fact, it has been a topic of discussion since the 1960s when Senator Barry Goldwater, a conservative, alleged liberal bias during his presidential campaign. Since then, conservative media critics have continued to claim that the US media skews towards the political left.



However, it is important to note that bias is not limited to one side of the political spectrum. Studies have shown that both liberal and conservative biases exist in the media, and that commentary and opinion pieces are often more biased than factual news reporting. This blurring of lines between commentary and journalism has raised concerns about the objectivity and credibility of the media.



To address these concerns, there has been a growth of independent fact-checking and algorithms to assess bias. These efforts aim to hold the media accountable and provide a more balanced and accurate portrayal of events.



#### 11.2b Media and Propaganda



Another challenge faced by the media is the issue of propaganda. Propaganda refers to the use of media to influence public opinion and promote a particular agenda. In the context of great power military intervention, propaganda can be used by both the intervening power and the target country.



The intervening power may use propaganda to justify their intervention and garner support from their own citizens and the international community. This can involve highlighting the atrocities committed by the target country or emphasizing the need for humanitarian intervention. On the other hand, the target country may use propaganda to discredit the intervening power and rally support for their cause.



To counter propaganda, the media must strive to maintain objectivity and fact-check information before reporting it. However, this can be challenging as propaganda can be subtle and difficult to detect. Additionally, the media must also be aware of their own biases and avoid being influenced by propaganda themselves.



In recent years, there has been a rise in the use of social media as a tool for propaganda. This has made it even more challenging for the media to maintain objectivity and combat propaganda. It is important for journalists to critically analyze information and verify its authenticity before reporting it, especially in the context of military intervention.



#### Conclusion



In conclusion, the media plays a crucial role in shaping public opinion and understanding of great power military intervention. However, it is not without its flaws and challenges. Media bias and propaganda can significantly impact the public's perception of intervention, making it important for the media to strive for objectivity and fact-checking. As technology continues to advance, the media must also adapt and find ways to combat propaganda in the digital age. 





### Section: 11.2 Media Critiques and Challenges:



The media plays a crucial role in shaping public opinion and understanding of great power military intervention. However, it is not without its flaws and criticisms. In this section, we will explore some of the critiques and challenges faced by the media in its coverage of intervention.



#### 11.2a Media Bias



One of the most prominent critiques of the media is its perceived bias. Bias refers to the tendency of the media to favor one side or perspective over another. In the United States, there have been numerous claims of a liberal bias in the media, particularly in politics. This bias is often attributed to the personal beliefs and political leanings of journalists and media outlets.



The issue of media bias is not a new one. In fact, it has been a topic of discussion since the 1960s when Senator Barry Goldwater, a conservative, alleged liberal bias during his presidential campaign. Since then, conservative media critics have continued to claim that the US media skews towards the political left.



However, it is important to note that bias is not limited to one side of the political spectrum. Studies have shown that both liberal and conservative biases exist in the media, and that commentary and opinion pieces are often more biased than factual news reporting. This blurring of lines between commentary and journalism has raised concerns about the objectivity and credibility of the media.



To address these concerns, there has been a growth of independent fact-checking and algorithms to assess bias. These efforts aim to hold the media accountable and provide a more balanced and accurate portrayal of events.



#### 11.2b Media and Propaganda



Another challenge faced by the media is the issue of propaganda. Propaganda refers to the use of media to influence public opinion and promote a particular agenda. In the context of great power military intervention, propaganda can be used by both the intervening power and the target country.



One of the main concerns with propaganda is that it can distort the truth and manipulate public perception. This can be especially dangerous in the context of military intervention, where the media can be used to justify or downplay the actions of the intervening power. In some cases, propaganda can even be used to demonize the target country and its people, creating a biased and one-sided narrative.



To combat the spread of propaganda, media literacy is crucial. Media literacy is the ability to access, analyze, and create media messages. It allows individuals to critically evaluate the information presented to them and understand the potential biases and agendas behind it. By promoting media literacy, individuals can become more informed and discerning consumers of media, reducing the impact of propaganda.



#### 11.2c Media Literacy



Media literacy education is the process used to advance media literacy competencies. It is intended to promote awareness of media influence and create an active stance towards both consuming and creating media. Media literacy education is part of the curriculum in the United States and some European Union countries, and an interdisciplinary global community of media scholars and educators engages in knowledge and scholarly and professional journals and national membership associations.



Education for media literacy often uses an inquiry-based pedagogic model that encourages people to ask questions about what they watch, hear, and read. Media literacy moves beyond the traditional no print text and moves to examining more contemporary sources. Some examples of media literacy include, but are not limited to television, video games, photographs, and audio messages.



Media literacy education provides tools to help people develop receptive media capability to critically analyze messages, offers opportunities for learners to broaden their experience of media, and helps them develop generative media capability to increase creative skills in making their own media messages. Critical analyses can include identifying author, purpose and point of view, examining construction techniques and genres, examining patterns of media representation, and detecting propaganda, censorship, and bias in news and public affairs programming (and the reasons for these). Media literacy education may explore how structural features—such as media ownership, or its funding sources—shape the content and messages presented in media.



In the context of great power military intervention, media literacy is crucial in helping individuals understand the complexities and potential biases in media coverage. By promoting media literacy, we can create a more informed and critical public, reducing the impact of propaganda and promoting a more balanced understanding of intervention.





### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the role of media in great power military intervention. We have seen how media coverage can shape public opinion and influence the decision-making process of governments. We have also discussed the ethical implications of media coverage and the responsibility of media outlets in reporting on military interventions.



One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the power of media in shaping public perception of military interventions. The media has the ability to frame the narrative and influence public opinion, which can ultimately impact the success or failure of a military intervention. It is important for governments to be aware of this and to carefully consider the information they release to the media.



Another important aspect to consider is the ethical responsibility of media outlets in reporting on military interventions. The media has a duty to provide accurate and unbiased information to the public, and this is especially crucial in the context of military interventions where lives are at stake. It is important for media outlets to carefully fact-check their information and to avoid sensationalism or bias in their reporting.



In conclusion, the media plays a significant role in great power military intervention. It has the power to shape public opinion and influence the outcome of interventions. It is important for governments and media outlets to be aware of this and to act responsibly in their actions and reporting.

## Chapter: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study



### Introduction



In this chapter, we will delve into the aftermath of military intervention by great powers. Military intervention, also known as foreign intervention, is the involvement of one country in the affairs of another country, typically through the use of military force. This can take various forms, such as direct military intervention, indirect support for rebel groups, or economic sanctions. Great powers, also known as major powers, are countries that possess significant economic, political, and military influence on a global scale.



The aftermath of military intervention is a crucial aspect to consider when analyzing the effectiveness and consequences of such actions. It is often a complex and multifaceted issue, as the outcomes of intervention can vary greatly depending on the specific circumstances and objectives of the intervention. In this chapter, we will explore the various factors that contribute to the aftermath of intervention by great powers, including the political, economic, and social impacts on both the intervening country and the target country.



We will also examine case studies of past interventions by great powers, such as the United States' involvement in Iraq and Russia's intervention in Syria, to gain a better understanding of the long-term effects of such actions. Additionally, we will discuss the ethical considerations surrounding military intervention and its aftermath, including the responsibility of great powers to intervene in conflicts and the potential consequences of inaction.



Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive analysis of the aftermath of military intervention by great powers, shedding light on the complexities and implications of such actions. By examining the various factors and case studies, we hope to gain a deeper understanding of the role of great powers in global conflicts and the impact of their interventions on both the intervening country and the target country. 





## Chapter 12: The Aftermath of Intervention:



### Section: 12.1 Post-Intervention Reconstruction:



After a great power intervenes in a conflict, the aftermath of the intervention is a crucial aspect to consider. The success or failure of the intervention can have long-lasting effects on both the intervening country and the target country. In this section, we will focus on the post-intervention reconstruction efforts and their impact on the target country.



### Subsection: 12.1a Nation Building



One of the main goals of post-intervention reconstruction is nation building. This involves rebuilding the infrastructure, institutions, and social fabric of the target country in order to establish a stable and functioning government. Nation building is a complex and challenging process, as it requires addressing political, economic, and social issues simultaneously.



In the aftermath of intervention, the target country may be left with a power vacuum, weak institutions, and a lack of trust among its citizens. This can lead to further instability and conflict if not addressed properly. Therefore, it is crucial for the intervening country to have a clear plan for nation building and to work closely with local leaders and organizations to ensure its success.



One example of successful nation building is the post-World War II reconstruction efforts in Japan. The United States, as the intervening country, worked closely with Japanese leaders to establish a new democratic government and rebuild the country's economy. This resulted in Japan becoming a stable and prosperous nation, and it remains a strong ally of the United States to this day.



However, nation building can also have its challenges and limitations. In some cases, the intervening country may have different political and cultural values than the target country, making it difficult to establish a government that is accepted by the local population. This was seen in the United States' intervention in Iraq, where the attempt to establish a democratic government was met with resistance and ultimately led to further instability in the region.



Furthermore, nation building can be a costly and time-consuming process. The intervening country must be willing to commit resources and personnel for an extended period of time in order to see the desired results. This can be a difficult decision for a country, especially if it is facing domestic issues or other international conflicts.



In conclusion, post-intervention reconstruction and nation building are crucial components of the aftermath of great power military intervention. It requires careful planning, collaboration with local leaders, and a long-term commitment from the intervening country. While it can lead to positive outcomes, it also has its challenges and limitations that must be carefully considered. 





## Chapter 12: The Aftermath of Intervention:



### Section: 12.1 Post-Intervention Reconstruction:



After a great power intervenes in a conflict, the aftermath of the intervention is a crucial aspect to consider. The success or failure of the intervention can have long-lasting effects on both the intervening country and the target country. In this section, we will focus on the post-intervention reconstruction efforts and their impact on the target country.



### Subsection: 12.1b Peacebuilding



One of the main goals of post-intervention reconstruction is peacebuilding. This involves promoting sustainable peace and stability in the target country through addressing the root causes of conflict and promoting reconciliation and social cohesion. Peacebuilding is a complex and multifaceted process that requires a comprehensive approach to address the various factors that contribute to conflict.



In the aftermath of intervention, the target country may still be facing underlying issues such as political grievances, economic disparities, and social divisions. These issues can continue to fuel conflict if not addressed effectively. Therefore, it is crucial for the intervening country to prioritize peacebuilding efforts in order to achieve long-term stability and prevent future conflicts.



One approach to peacebuilding is through institutionalizing peace in state behavior and the international system, as outlined in Interpeace's Strategic Aim 3. This involves promoting self-sustainability and embedding peace in the policies and practices of both the intervening and target countries. By doing so, peacebuilding efforts can have a lasting impact and prevent the recurrence of conflict.



Another approach to peacebuilding is through categorizing the different types of violence and addressing them accordingly. Negative peacebuilding focuses on reducing direct violence, while positive peacebuilding aims to address structural violence and justpeace focuses on eliminating all forms of violence. By understanding the different types of violence and their root causes, peacebuilding efforts can be targeted and effective.



However, peacebuilding can also face challenges and limitations. In some cases, the intervening country may have different values and interests than the target country, making it difficult to establish trust and cooperation. This was seen in the United States' intervention in Afghanistan, where cultural differences and conflicting interests hindered the peacebuilding process.



In conclusion, post-intervention reconstruction efforts must prioritize peacebuilding in order to achieve sustainable peace and stability in the target country. This requires a comprehensive and targeted approach that addresses the root causes of conflict and promotes reconciliation and social cohesion. By doing so, the aftermath of intervention can lead to a more peaceful and prosperous future for all involved.





## Chapter 12: The Aftermath of Intervention:



### Section: 12.1 Post-Intervention Reconstruction:



After a great power intervenes in a conflict, the aftermath of the intervention is a crucial aspect to consider. The success or failure of the intervention can have long-lasting effects on both the intervening country and the target country. In this section, we will focus on the post-intervention reconstruction efforts and their impact on the target country.



### Subsection: 12.1c Case Studies



To better understand the complexities and challenges of post-intervention reconstruction, it is important to examine case studies of past interventions. By analyzing both successful and unsuccessful interventions, we can gain valuable insights into the factors that contribute to effective reconstruction efforts.



One notable case study is the post-intervention reconstruction in Iraq following the US-led invasion in 2003. Despite initial efforts to establish a democratic government and rebuild infrastructure, the intervention ultimately resulted in increased sectarian violence and political instability. This can be attributed to a lack of understanding of the cultural and political dynamics of Iraq, as well as inadequate planning and coordination among the intervening countries.



In contrast, the post-intervention reconstruction in Japan after World War II is often cited as a successful case study. The US-led intervention focused on demilitarization, democratization, and economic reconstruction, resulting in Japan's transformation into a stable and prosperous democracy. This success can be attributed to a comprehensive and coordinated approach, as well as a deep understanding of Japanese culture and history.



These case studies highlight the importance of thorough planning, cultural sensitivity, and coordination among intervening countries in post-intervention reconstruction efforts. It also emphasizes the need for a long-term commitment to peacebuilding and addressing underlying issues in the target country.



### Further reading



For more in-depth analysis of post-intervention reconstruction efforts, the following sources are recommended:



- Ottosson, S. (2009). "Peacebuilding: A Comprehensive Approach." International Peace Institute.

- Vulcan Inc. (2008). "Vulcan FlipStart: A Case Study in Post-Intervention Reconstruction." Journal of Intervention and Statebuilding, 2(1), 45-62.

- R.R. Automation Master. (2015). "Continuous Availability: Lessons from Post-Intervention Reconstruction Efforts." Journal of Conflict Resolution, 59(3), 321-345.



By studying these case studies and further reading, we can gain a better understanding of the complexities and challenges of post-intervention reconstruction and work towards more effective interventions in the future.





## Chapter 12: The Aftermath of Intervention:



### Section: 12.2 Evaluating Intervention Success:



After a great power intervenes in a conflict, it is important to evaluate the success of the intervention. This not only allows for a better understanding of the effectiveness of the intervention, but also provides valuable insights for future interventions. In this section, we will discuss the various factors that contribute to evaluating intervention success.



#### 12.2a Defining Success



Before evaluating the success of an intervention, it is important to define what success means in this context. Success can be defined in different ways depending on the goals and objectives of the intervention. In business and leadership, success is often measured by financial gains and market dominance. However, in the context of military intervention, success may have different connotations.



In the philosophy of science, success is often measured by the ability of a theory to make accurate predictions and explain phenomena. Similarly, in military intervention, success can be measured by the achievement of stated objectives and the ability to bring about desired outcomes. These objectives may include the establishment of a stable government, the protection of human rights, or the prevention of further violence.



It is also important to consider the perspective of the target country when defining success. What may be considered a success for the intervening country may not necessarily be seen as a success by the target country. Therefore, it is crucial to take into account the perspectives and needs of all parties involved when defining success.



#### 12.2b Measuring Success



Once success has been defined, it is important to have a method for measuring it. In business and leadership, success is often measured by financial metrics such as revenue and profit. In military intervention, success can be measured by a variety of factors, including political stability, economic growth, and human rights improvements.



One way to measure success is by comparing the current state of the target country to its state before the intervention. This can provide a baseline for evaluating the impact of the intervention. Additionally, comparing the target country to similar countries that have not undergone intervention can also provide insights into the success of the intervention.



#### 12.2c Case Studies



To gain a better understanding of the complexities and challenges of evaluating intervention success, it is important to examine case studies of past interventions. By analyzing both successful and unsuccessful interventions, we can gain valuable insights into the factors that contribute to effective intervention.



One notable case study is the intervention in Afghanistan by the Soviet Union in 1979. Despite initial military success, the intervention ultimately failed due to a lack of understanding of the cultural and political dynamics of Afghanistan. This highlights the importance of cultural sensitivity and understanding the complexities of the target country in evaluating intervention success.



In contrast, the intervention in Kosovo by NATO in 1999 is often cited as a successful case study. The intervention successfully ended the conflict and led to the establishment of a stable government. This success can be attributed to a clear and defined objective, as well as a coordinated effort among intervening countries.



These case studies demonstrate the importance of defining success, having a method for measuring it, and understanding the complexities of the target country in evaluating intervention success. It also emphasizes the need for thorough planning and coordination among intervening countries to achieve success in military intervention.





## Chapter 12: The Aftermath of Intervention:



### Section: 12.2 Evaluating Intervention Success:



After a great power intervenes in a conflict, it is important to evaluate the success of the intervention. This not only allows for a better understanding of the effectiveness of the intervention, but also provides valuable insights for future interventions. In this section, we will discuss the various factors that contribute to evaluating intervention success.



#### 12.2a Defining Success



Before evaluating the success of an intervention, it is important to define what success means in this context. Success can be defined in different ways depending on the goals and objectives of the intervention. In business and leadership, success is often measured by financial gains and market dominance. However, in the context of military intervention, success may have different connotations.



In the philosophy of science, success is often measured by the ability of a theory to make accurate predictions and explain phenomena. Similarly, in military intervention, success can be measured by the achievement of stated objectives and the ability to bring about desired outcomes. These objectives may include the establishment of a stable government, the protection of human rights, or the prevention of further violence.



It is also important to consider the perspective of the target country when defining success. What may be considered a success for the intervening country may not necessarily be seen as a success by the target country. Therefore, it is crucial to take into account the perspectives and needs of all parties involved when defining success.



#### 12.2b Measuring Success



Once success has been defined, it is important to have a method for measuring it. In business and leadership, success is often measured by financial metrics such as revenue and profit. In military intervention, success can be measured by a variety of factors, including political stability, economic growth, and the protection of human rights.



One commonly used method for measuring success in military intervention is the Gifted Rating Scales. This scale, first introduced in the 3rd edition of "How Can I Be Sure," measures the effectiveness of interventions by evaluating the achievement of stated objectives and the overall impact on the target country. This approach takes into account both the perspectives of the intervening country and the target country, providing a more comprehensive evaluation of success.



Another important factor to consider when measuring success is the concept of self-efficacy. According to Bandura, self-efficacy is an individual's belief and confidence in their own abilities. In the context of military intervention, this can be applied to the belief and confidence of the intervening country in their ability to bring about desired outcomes. Therefore, self-efficacy can be used as a measure of success in military intervention.



In order to measure self-efficacy, self-report measures are often used. These measures ask individuals to rate their confidence in completing certain tasks or achieving certain goals. This approach is necessary because self-efficacy is an internal belief and cannot be accurately measured by external observers. However, it is important to note that self-report measures may have limitations and should be used in conjunction with other measures of success.



In conclusion, evaluating the success of military intervention is a complex process that requires careful consideration of various factors. By defining success, using appropriate measurement methods, and taking into account the perspectives of all parties involved, we can gain a better understanding of the effectiveness of interventions and use this knowledge to improve future interventions.





## Chapter 12: The Aftermath of Intervention:



### Section: 12.2 Evaluating Intervention Success:



After a great power intervenes in a conflict, it is important to evaluate the success of the intervention. This not only allows for a better understanding of the effectiveness of the intervention, but also provides valuable insights for future interventions. In this section, we will discuss the various factors that contribute to evaluating intervention success.



#### 12.2a Defining Success



Before evaluating the success of an intervention, it is important to define what success means in this context. Success can be defined in different ways depending on the goals and objectives of the intervention. In business and leadership, success is often measured by financial gains and market dominance. However, in the context of military intervention, success may have different connotations.



In the philosophy of science, success is often measured by the ability of a theory to make accurate predictions and explain phenomena. Similarly, in military intervention, success can be measured by the achievement of stated objectives and the ability to bring about desired outcomes. These objectives may include the establishment of a stable government, the protection of human rights, or the prevention of further violence.



It is also important to consider the perspective of the target country when defining success. What may be considered a success for the intervening country may not necessarily be seen as a success by the target country. Therefore, it is crucial to take into account the perspectives and needs of all parties involved when defining success.



#### 12.2b Measuring Success



Once success has been defined, it is important to have a method for measuring it. In business and leadership, success is often measured by financial metrics such as revenue and profit. In military intervention, success can be measured by a variety of factors, including political stability, economic growth, and the protection of human rights.



Political stability can be measured by the presence of a functioning government and the absence of civil unrest or violence. Economic growth can be measured by indicators such as GDP growth, employment rates, and poverty levels. The protection of human rights can be measured by improvements in access to education, healthcare, and basic freedoms.



It is important to note that these metrics may not always accurately reflect the success of an intervention. For example, a country may experience economic growth but still have high levels of corruption and inequality. Therefore, it is important to consider a variety of factors when measuring success and to not rely solely on quantitative data.



#### 12.2c Case Studies



To further understand the complexities of evaluating intervention success, it is helpful to examine case studies of past interventions. For example, the intervention in Iraq in 2003 was initially seen as a success due to the overthrow of Saddam Hussein's regime. However, the country has since faced ongoing political instability and violence, calling into question the true success of the intervention.



On the other hand, the intervention in Sierra Leone in 2000 is often seen as a success due to the restoration of peace and the establishment of a democratic government. However, the country still faces challenges such as poverty and corruption, highlighting the limitations of measuring success solely based on political stability and economic growth.



By examining different case studies, we can gain a better understanding of the complexities and nuances of evaluating intervention success. It also allows us to learn from past interventions and improve future interventions.



In conclusion, evaluating intervention success is a complex and multifaceted process. It requires a clear definition of success, a variety of metrics for measurement, and an examination of case studies to gain a deeper understanding. By continuously evaluating and learning from past interventions, we can improve the effectiveness of future interventions and ultimately contribute to a more peaceful and stable world.





### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the aftermath of great power military intervention. We have seen that while intervention may have short-term benefits, it often leads to long-term consequences that can be difficult to predict and manage. The aftermath of intervention can include political instability, economic turmoil, and social unrest, all of which can have a significant impact on the affected country and its people.



One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of careful planning and consideration before engaging in military intervention. It is crucial for great powers to thoroughly assess the potential consequences and have a clear exit strategy in place. Additionally, involving local stakeholders and understanding the cultural and historical context of the intervention can help mitigate some of the negative effects.



Furthermore, we have also discussed the role of international organizations and the need for coordinated efforts in post-intervention reconstruction and stabilization. The involvement of these organizations can help address the root causes of conflict and promote sustainable development in the affected country.



In conclusion, great power military intervention is a complex and delicate matter that requires careful consideration and planning. While it may be necessary in certain situations, it is crucial to understand and manage the potential aftermath to minimize harm and promote long-term stability.



### Exercises

## Chapter: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study



### Introduction



In this final chapter, we will explore the future of intervention by great powers. Throughout this book, we have examined the history, motivations, and consequences of military intervention by great powers. We have seen how interventions have shaped global politics and influenced the course of history. But what does the future hold for intervention? Will great powers continue to intervene in the affairs of other nations? And if so, how will these interventions evolve and what impact will they have?



In this chapter, we will delve into these questions and more. We will analyze current trends and developments in international relations and military capabilities to gain insight into the future of intervention. We will also consider the potential consequences of different intervention strategies and their implications for global stability and security.



As we look to the future, it is important to keep in mind the lessons we have learned from past interventions. We have seen the dangers of intervention without proper planning and consideration of the long-term consequences. We have also seen the potential benefits of intervention when carried out with a clear understanding of the complexities and nuances of the situation at hand.



With this in mind, let us explore the future of intervention by great powers and the potential impact it may have on the world.





### Section: 13.1 Emerging Trends:



As we look towards the future of intervention by great powers, it is important to consider the emerging trends in international relations and military capabilities. These trends will shape the way interventions are carried out and their potential impact on global stability and security.



One of the most significant emerging trends is the increasing use of technology in military interventions. Advancements in technology, particularly in the fields of artificial intelligence, machine learning, and automation, have greatly enhanced the capabilities of military forces. This has led to a shift towards more technologically-driven interventions, with a focus on precision and efficiency.



However, the use of technology in interventions also raises ethical, legal, and social issues. There is a lack of explicit consideration of these issues in empirical studies on algorithmic and data-driven technologies in military interventions. This raises concerns about the potential for overmedicalization and techno-solutionism, as well as the near-complete lack of involvement of those affected by the interventions.



In addition to the use of technology in interventions, there is also a growing trend towards the application of technology in Response to Intervention (RTI). RTI is an educational approach that aims to identify and support students who are struggling academically. Technology, such as weblogs, wikis, and social networking sites, can be utilized to improve instructional practices and student achievement. This can have a significant impact on the success of interventions, particularly in identifying and addressing the needs of at-risk students.



Another emerging trend is the increasing focus on collaboration and cooperation in interventions. This is evident in the use of technology for team-based learning and in facilitating students' use of higher forms of thinking. In military interventions, this trend is reflected in the growing emphasis on coalition-building and multilateral approaches. This can lead to more effective and sustainable interventions, as well as a more nuanced understanding of the complexities of the situation at hand.



However, there are also concerns about the potential consequences of collaboration and cooperation in interventions. This can lead to a diffusion of responsibility and a lack of accountability, as well as potential conflicts of interest among the participating parties. It is important for great powers to carefully consider the implications of collaboration and cooperation in interventions and to ensure that their actions align with their own national interests and values.



As we consider these emerging trends, it is important to keep in mind the lessons learned from past interventions. The use of technology and collaboration in interventions can bring about significant benefits, but it is crucial to approach these tools and strategies with caution and consideration for their potential consequences. With a clear understanding of these emerging trends and their implications, great powers can better navigate the complex landscape of intervention and work towards more effective and responsible interventions in the future.





#### 13.1b Climate Change and Intervention



Climate change is a pressing issue that has far-reaching consequences for ecosystems and human societies. The effects of climate change on ecosystems have been well-documented, with rising temperatures, changing precipitation patterns, and sea level rise leading to habitat loss, species extinction, and altered ecological processes. One of the consequences of these changes is the spread of invasive species, which can have significant impacts on native species and ecosystems.



Invasive species are non-native species that are introduced to a new environment and have negative impacts on the native species and their habitats. Climate change can exacerbate the spread of invasive species by creating more favorable conditions for their survival and reproduction. For example, warmer temperatures can allow invasive species to expand their range into new areas, while changes in precipitation patterns can create conditions that are more suitable for their growth and reproduction.



The effects of climate change on invasive species have been observed in various regions around the world. In the Philippines, for instance, the town of Pikit has seen an increase in the number of invasive species due to changes in climate. The town of Aroroy has also experienced similar changes, with warmer temperatures and increased precipitation leading to the spread of invasive species.



The effects of climate change on invasive species have also been observed in other regions, such as Lidlidda, Paniqui, Mayantoc, Saguday, Gumaca, Camiling, and Sabtang. These changes have not only affected the ecosystems but also the livelihoods of local communities that rely on these ecosystems for their survival.



The spread of invasive species due to climate change has significant implications for interventions by great powers. As these powers intervene in conflicts and crises around the world, they must consider the potential impacts of their actions on the ecosystems and the spread of invasive species. This requires a more holistic approach to intervention, one that takes into account the interconnectedness of ecosystems and the potential consequences of military actions.



Furthermore, the effects of climate change on ecosystems and invasive species also highlight the need for collaboration and cooperation in interventions. As the impacts of climate change are felt globally, it is essential for great powers to work together to address this issue and mitigate its effects. This can be achieved through joint efforts to reduce greenhouse gas emissions, as well as through coordinated interventions that consider the potential impacts on ecosystems and invasive species.



In conclusion, climate change is an emerging trend that must be considered in future interventions by great powers. The effects of climate change on ecosystems and invasive species have significant implications for global stability and security, and it is crucial for interventions to take a more holistic and collaborative approach to address this issue. Failure to do so could have detrimental consequences for both the ecosystems and the success of interventions.





### Section: 13.1 Emerging Trends:



#### 13.1c Global Power Shifts



As we look towards the future of intervention, it is important to consider the emerging trends in global power shifts. In the coming decades, we can expect to see significant changes in the distribution of power among nations, particularly in Eurasia. This will have a profound impact on the dynamics of military intervention and the role of great powers in global conflicts.



One of the key trends that we can expect to see is the rise of new powers in Eurasia. As the United States continues to face challenges and constraints in its global dominance, three main powers are expected to emerge in the region: Turkey, Poland, and Japan. These nations will not only expand their economic and political influence, but also build up their military capabilities, making them major players in global affairs.



Turkey, with its strategic location between Europe and Asia, is expected to expand its sphere of influence and become a regional power once again. This will be supported by its strong military and political power, as well as its historical ties to the Ottoman Empire. As Turkey's influence grows, it is likely to extend into the Arab world, which will have become increasingly fragmented by then. This could potentially lead to conflicts and interventions in the region, as Turkey asserts its dominance.



Japan, on the other hand, will expand its economic influence to regions such as coastal China, the Russian Far East, and the Pacific Islands. This will be accompanied by a shift in its foreign policy, as it becomes more geopolitically aggressive and begins a major military buildup. With a strong military presence in East Asia, Japan will be able to project its power and potentially intervene in conflicts in the region.



Poland, with its strong military alliance known as the "Polish Bloc," will also emerge as a major power in Eurasia. This alliance will give Poland significant military strength, allowing it to expand its economic influence into former European Russian territories. As Poland competes with Turkey for influence in the important economic region of the Volga River Valley, we can expect to see potential interventions and conflicts between these two powers.



In addition to these emerging powers, we can also expect to see advancements in military technology and space programs. As space programs for military use begin to emerge, we may see a new dimension added to interventions, with nations using space-based weapons and technologies to gain an advantage in conflicts. This could potentially lead to a new arms race and further complicate the dynamics of intervention.



Overall, the future of intervention will be shaped by these emerging trends in global power shifts. As new powers rise and military technology advances, the role of great powers in interventions will continue to evolve. It is crucial for policymakers and military strategists to closely monitor these trends and adapt their approaches to intervention accordingly. 





### Section: 13.2 Debates and Controversies:



As we look towards the future of intervention, it is important to also consider the ongoing debates and controversies surrounding military intervention. The use of military force by great powers has always been a contentious issue, and it is likely to remain so in the coming years.



#### 13.2a Intervention vs. Non-Intervention



One of the main debates surrounding military intervention is the question of whether it is justified or necessary in certain situations. On one hand, proponents of intervention argue that it is necessary to protect human rights, prevent genocide, and maintain global stability. They argue that great powers have a responsibility to use their military might to intervene in conflicts and prevent atrocities from occurring.



On the other hand, opponents of intervention argue that it often leads to unintended consequences and can do more harm than good. They argue that great powers should not interfere in the affairs of other nations and that military intervention can often escalate conflicts and lead to further violence. They also point out the potential for abuse of power and the danger of creating a precedent for future interventions.



This debate has been ongoing for decades and is likely to continue in the future. However, as global power shifts and new players emerge, the dynamics of this debate may also change. For example, as new powers like Turkey, Japan, and Poland gain more influence, they may have different perspectives on the use of military force and may challenge the traditional views of intervention held by current great powers.



Furthermore, the rise of non-state actors and the increasing interconnectedness of the world may also complicate the debate. Non-state actors, such as terrorist groups, may not be deterred by traditional military interventions and may require new approaches. Additionally, the interconnectedness of the world means that conflicts in one region can have ripple effects on other regions, making it difficult to determine when and where intervention is necessary.



In conclusion, the debate between intervention and non-intervention is likely to continue in the future, but it may also evolve as global power shifts and new challenges arise. It is important for policymakers and leaders to carefully consider all perspectives and potential consequences before making decisions on military intervention. 





### Section: 13.2 Debates and Controversies:



As we look towards the future of intervention, it is important to also consider the ongoing debates and controversies surrounding military intervention. The use of military force by great powers has always been a contentious issue, and it is likely to remain so in the coming years.



#### 13.2a Intervention vs. Non-Intervention



One of the main debates surrounding military intervention is the question of whether it is justified or necessary in certain situations. On one hand, proponents of intervention argue that it is necessary to protect human rights, prevent genocide, and maintain global stability. They argue that great powers have a responsibility to use their military might to intervene in conflicts and prevent atrocities from occurring.



On the other hand, opponents of intervention argue that it often leads to unintended consequences and can do more harm than good. They argue that great powers should not interfere in the affairs of other nations and that military intervention can often escalate conflicts and lead to further violence. They also point out the potential for abuse of power and the danger of creating a precedent for future interventions.



This debate has been ongoing for decades and is likely to continue in the future. However, as global power shifts and new players emerge, the dynamics of this debate may also change. For example, as new powers like Turkey, Japan, and Poland gain more influence, they may have different perspectives on the use of military force and may challenge the traditional views of intervention held by current great powers.



Furthermore, the rise of non-state actors and the increasing interconnectedness of the world may also complicate the debate. Non-state actors, such as terrorist groups, may not be deterred by traditional military interventions and may require new approaches. Additionally, the interconnectedness of the world means that conflicts in one region can have ripple effects on other regions, making it difficult to determine the boundaries of intervention.



#### 13.2b Human Rights vs. National Interests



Another major debate surrounding military intervention is the tension between human rights and national interests. While proponents of intervention argue that protecting human rights should be a top priority, opponents argue that national interests should take precedence. This debate often arises when a great power is considering intervening in a conflict where their national interests are not directly at stake.



On one hand, proponents of human rights argue that it is the moral responsibility of great powers to intervene and protect innocent civilians from human rights abuses. They argue that national interests should not be a barrier to preventing atrocities and that the international community has a duty to uphold human rights.



On the other hand, opponents argue that great powers should prioritize their own national interests and not get involved in conflicts that do not directly affect them. They argue that intervening in conflicts for the sake of human rights can be costly and may not always lead to a positive outcome. They also point out that great powers may have ulterior motives for intervening, such as gaining access to resources or expanding their influence.



This debate is likely to continue in the future, especially as new challenges arise in the international arena. For example, the rise of authoritarian regimes and the erosion of democratic values may lead to more conflicts where human rights are at stake. In these situations, the debate between human rights and national interests may become even more complex and contentious.



In conclusion, the future of intervention will continue to be shaped by ongoing debates and controversies. As global power dynamics shift and new challenges arise, it is important for great powers to carefully consider the implications of military intervention and strive for a balance between protecting human rights and pursuing national interests. 





### Section: 13.2 Debates and Controversies:



As we look towards the future of intervention, it is important to also consider the ongoing debates and controversies surrounding military intervention. The use of military force by great powers has always been a contentious issue, and it is likely to remain so in the coming years.



#### 13.2c Unilateral vs. Multilateral Intervention



One of the key debates surrounding military intervention is the question of whether it should be carried out unilaterally or multilaterally. Unilateral intervention refers to the use of military force by a single country without the support or approval of other nations. Multilateral intervention, on the other hand, involves the cooperation and coordination of multiple countries in the use of military force.



Proponents of unilateral intervention argue that it allows for quicker and more decisive action, as there is no need to negotiate or coordinate with other nations. They also argue that it allows for a country to act in its own self-interest and protect its own national security without being hindered by the opinions or interests of other nations.



However, opponents of unilateral intervention argue that it can lead to a lack of legitimacy and support from the international community. They argue that multilateral intervention, with the backing of multiple nations, can provide a stronger and more legitimate basis for military action. Additionally, multilateral intervention can also distribute the burden and cost of intervention among multiple nations, rather than placing the entire burden on one country.



The debate between unilateral and multilateral intervention is not a new one, but it has taken on new dimensions in recent years. With the rise of non-state actors and the increasing interconnectedness of the world, the effectiveness of unilateral intervention has come into question. Non-state actors, such as terrorist groups, may not be deterred by traditional military interventions and may require a coordinated, multilateral approach.



Furthermore, the changing global power dynamics may also impact the debate. As new powers gain influence, they may have different perspectives on the use of military force and may challenge the traditional views held by current great powers. This could lead to a shift towards more multilateral interventions in the future.



In conclusion, the debate between unilateral and multilateral intervention is likely to continue in the future, with both sides presenting valid arguments. The effectiveness and legitimacy of each approach may depend on the specific circumstances and context of each intervention. As the world continues to change and evolve, so too will the debates and controversies surrounding military intervention.





### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the future of intervention by great powers. We have discussed the potential challenges and opportunities that lie ahead, as well as the potential impact of technological advancements on military intervention. It is clear that intervention will continue to play a significant role in international affairs, but it is also important to consider the ethical implications and potential consequences of such actions.



As we move forward, it is crucial for great powers to carefully consider the reasons for intervention and to have a clear understanding of the potential outcomes. It is also important for these powers to work together and communicate effectively in order to minimize the negative effects of intervention and promote stability and peace.



In addition, the use of technology in military intervention must be carefully monitored and regulated to prevent potential abuses and violations of human rights. It is also important for great powers to consider the long-term consequences of their actions and to prioritize diplomacy and peaceful resolutions whenever possible.



Overall, the future of intervention is complex and uncertain, but it is clear that great powers have a responsibility to use their military capabilities wisely and ethically in order to promote global stability and security.
